nothyng meruaile see wonder worketh beholdeth place uenice standeth would imagine without buildyng habitacion shoulde saie rudest vnmeerest vnholsomest place builde vpon enhabite w • againe founde thoroughout whole worlde standeth open vpon maine sea foure mile neerest maine lande suche marishe euery low water leaueth muddy ground vncouered euery full sea drowneth cleane yet men constreigned necessitee haue brought marishe suche passe onely excedyng full people riche treasure buildynges holesome withall throughe muche haunte people great noumbre continuall fyres thynke none citee hable stretcheth towardꝭ citee concordia 60 myles length dooeth defende water floudde within marishes hath nothyng lyke force sea costes great mattier whan sea swelleth uenice iiii v foote aboue lowe water marke notwithstandyng citee seemeth rather part sea marisshe euerie chanell woulde saie euery streete full water chanels many maie row partes citee though way also goe land list whiche streetes parte verie narow house nothyng faire water side marisshe betwene citee maine lande whan water low parte chanels shalow botes haue muche dooe passe fro mudde encreaseth daiely reason lande flouddes noumbre riuers fallyng dooe carie theim wonderfull treasure uenetians spend continuall diggyng cariyng awaie mudde preserue theyr foresaied chanelles defende theyr citee ioygne maine lande ¶the banke rehersed broken vii place whiche botes maie come shippe passe uenice sauyng porte malamoco two castelles lio entrie wherof daungerous reason sandꝭ mouable whan shippe cometh taketh fyrst pilottes sounde waie whiche effect reputed one greatest surety uenetians haue defence theyr citee ennemies sea lande impossible hurt besiege vnlesse enemie hable occupie 150 myle compasse armie buildynges nexte vnto
